  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_3f963ca8-414f-4db8-80fd-19d55b368a87'
      });
    }

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer2222544542982956593">Vlad Taltos ist ein Hexer, freiberuflicher Attentäter, lebt als Ostländer (also Mensch) unter Dragaeranern und nennt einen reptilischen Vertrauten mit beissendem Humor sein Eigen. Und er ist in Schwierigkeiten, denn er muss einen Krieg verhindern, in dem sich seine besten Freunde und daneben auch die großen Familien von Dragaera gegenseitig auslöschen würden...<br/><br/>The first to</span>
  <span id="freeText2222544542982956593" style="display:none">Vlad Taltos ist ein Hexer, freiberuflicher Attentäter, lebt als Ostländer (also Mensch) unter Dragaeranern und nennt einen reptilischen Vertrauten mit beissendem Humor sein Eigen. Und er ist in Schwierigkeiten, denn er muss einen Krieg verhindern, in dem sich seine besten Freunde und daneben auch die großen Familien von Dragaera gegenseitig auslöschen würden...<br /><br />The first to be published, this is actually the fourth novel in the timeline of the VLAD TALTOS series. The books recount the adventures of the wisecracking hired killer Vlad, a human on a planet mainly inhabited by the long-lived, extremely tall sorcerers known as the Dragaerans. One of the most powerful bosses in the Jhereg--Dragaera's premier criminal organization--hires Vlad, one of their guild members, to assassinate Mellar, who stole millions from the Jhereg leadership and fled. Unfortunately, this thief turns out to be protected in a way that makes it difficult for Vlad to do his job without gaining the permanent enmity of a friend. The reader also learns more about Vlad's past in this, and in other, lives.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2222544542982956593" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/627969-so-this-book-is-actually-the-4th-is-it">So this book is actually the 4th...
Is it still supposed to be read first, and if not, in what order?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_627969'><a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F133454.Jhereg">like</a></span>

</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionTimestamp'>
<a href="/questions/627969-so-this-book-is-actually-the-4th-is-it">4 years ago</a>
</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionPermalink'>
<a href="/questions/627969-so-this-book-is-actually-the-4th-is-it">Add your answer</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>

</div>
<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/7973025-dan-l"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1330479044i/7973025._UY100_CR16,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/7973025-dan-l">Dan&#39;l</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Order of publication. Later books, even when he is careful, sometimes build on what has already been revealed, and several momentous plot points will <a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Order of publication. Later books, even when he is careful, sometimes build on what has already been revealed, and several momentous plot points will be lessened if read out of publication order. I won't say what or which books - that gives too much away.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

<div class='communityQuestionAndAnswer'>
<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/536484-should-i-read-this-series-in-order-of">Should I read this series in order of publishing, or in chronological order? What would you recommend?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_536484'><a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F133454.Jhereg">like</a></span>

</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionTimestamp'>
<a href="/questions/536484-should-i-read-this-series-in-order-of">5 years ago</a>
</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionPermalink'>
<a href="/questions/536484-should-i-read-this-series-in-order-of">Add your answer</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>

</div>
<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/7973025-dan-l"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1330479044i/7973025._UY100_CR16,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/7973025-dan-l">Dan&#39;l</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Order of publication is best. The reason being, as much as Steve might foreshadow, really, the later books inevitably build upon what is established i<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Order of publication is best. The reason being, as much as Steve might foreshadow, really, the later books inevitably build upon what is established in the early books. You are getting the events out of chronological order, but in the order that Steve (or, within the larger frame story, Vlad) chose to tell them. Also, some developments later in the series will lack the impact they should have, without knowing the relevant characters from earlier books.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerFooter'>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_459150907" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/459150907" />
    <a title="Bookwraiths" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14716035-bookwraiths"><img alt="Bookwraiths" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1353765210p2/14716035.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/459150907?book_show_action=true">Nov 19, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bookwraiths" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bookwraiths" href="/user/show/14716035-bookwraiths">Bookwraiths</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780441385546" href="/book/show/1281575.Jhereg">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14716035-bookwraiths?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer459150907" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1312713300437525759">Originally reviewed at <a href='http://bookwraiths.com/2014/11/21/flashback-friday-jhereg-vlad-taltos-1-by-steven-brust/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Bookwraiths</a>. <br/><br/>I read this novel when it was initially published in the mid-80s. It was a favorite of mine at the time, and I have always recalled it fondly. However, after completing a re-read, it has become painfully obvious that the enjoyment I received from this book must have been one of those teenage fads because . . . it has disappeared right along with my desire to keep solving a Rubik’s Cube.<br/><br/>The tour guide in <i>Jhereg</i> is Vlad Taltos. The world he guides us through is </span>
  <span id="freeText1312713300437525759" style="display:none">Originally reviewed at <a href="http://bookwraiths.com/2014/11/21/flashback-friday-jhereg-vlad-taltos-1-by-steven-brust/" rel="nofollow noopener">Bookwraiths</a>. <br /><br />I read this novel when it was initially published in the mid-80s. It was a favorite of mine at the time, and I have always recalled it fondly. However, after completing a re-read, it has become painfully obvious that the enjoyment I received from this book must have been one of those teenage fads because . . . it has disappeared right along with my desire to keep solving a Rubik’s Cube.<br /><br />The tour guide in <i>Jhereg</i> is Vlad Taltos. The world he guides us through is a standard one from 80s fantasy. Here a huge Empire controls most of the world, inhabited and ruled by the Dragaerans, who are basically LoTR-like elves. Indeed, the few humans in this world often refer to the Dragaerans as “elves," though to “confuse” the reader a bit the author has the Dragaerans refer to themselves as “human.” Other than this one quirk, there is nothing to set it apart from other fantasy worlds from this period of the 80s.<br /><br />Vlad is one of the human minority of the Dragaeran Empire, labeled by his “elvish” overlords as an "Easterner" and born into the lowest class of society. However, thanks to a social-climbing father, Vlad is actually a citizen of the Empire and a noble of one of the lesser Dragaeran houses. (There are 17 Great Houses in Dragaeran; each named after an animal of the world.) Of course, the house Vlad is a noble of just happens to be one huge criminal organization, which greatly resembles the modern day Mafia. Our protagonist’s role in this elvish “mafia” is as a minor crime lord, supervising certain criminal interests of the “house,” and as an accomplished assassin. To throw in a little “fantastical,” the author also makes him a minor sorcerer. <br /><br />The novel itself starts out with Brust focusing on Vlad’s childhood, especially the story of how he acquires a live Jhereg egg, which later hatches out into his “familiar” Loiosh. (The golden reptile on the front cover of the paperback edition is Loiosh.) The two of them share a telepathic “link;” their constant bantering being the main comedic point of the book, though it does grow tiresome after a while. <br /><br />After this boyhood tale, Brust time warps ahead approximately seven years to the main action of the novel. (This fast forward effectively leapfrogging three of the subsequently books in the series, making this the fourth in chronological sequence I believe.) Here another “mob” boss hires Vlad to kill one of the Jhereg's higher-ups, who has disappeared with some money that doesn’t belong to him. The job has to be done quickly before word of this theft can get out and make the Jhereg look “weak.” <br /><br />Since Vlad is a skilled assassin, the job doesn’t seem like a big deal until he discovers that his target has taken refuge in Castle Black, as a guest of Morrolan the Dragon lord. Morrolan is a heavy-weight Dragon with bad mojo magic. Word is that this Dragon lord is such a tickler for honor that once he has taken someone into his home as a welcomed guest that they are under his protection, no matter what. Plus, Vlad has a professional relationship with Morrolan (a strange friendship even), which complicates everything.<br /><br />So now, the easy job has gotten complicated, and Vlad spends many pages planning the perfect assassination scheme. Ultimately, the plan boils down to this convoluted scheme to get the target out of Morrolan's house without using magic and without actually killing him inside the actual castle. (It is much more complicated and cumbersome than that; I’m just trying to make it easier to understand here.) Naturally, things fall apart, people have to improvise, the incident turns into a full blown political situation between the Jhereg and the Dragon houses, and then things get cleared up at the end.<br /><br /><b>PROS:</b> <br /><br />There are several nice things about this book, which many reads will no doubt enjoy. <br /><br /><b>1)</b> It is fast paced - mainly because it is very short - and is written in a flowing style that keeps the pace moving, never bogging down in descriptions or tiresome wordiness. <br /><br /><b>2)</b> It is also very modern in tone. The magic and other “fantasy” elements here are very straight forward, accepted by everyone in the story as part of every day life and never really discussed. Indeed, Jhereg is so modern in tone that it can just as readily be enjoyed as a contemporary mafia story rather than a fantasy; if the “fantasy” elements bore you, all one must do is just imagine it is all taking place in New York City as opposed to another world. <br /> <br /><b>3)</b> <i>Jhereg</i> is a fantasy detective or mafia story during a time when Tolkien clones were all the rage. So, at least in the early 80s, it was different. Not so much now but still good variety I suppose. <br /><br /><b>4)</b> The interaction between the men and women of the book is very business-like with a post-feminism flavor. No sexual discrimination here. Hell, no sex here. Lol! Nope, no sexist remarks about females in general or anything like that; everyone appears equal without any distinction between male or female. <br /><br /><b>CONS:</b> <br /><br /><b>1)</b> While this book is a fantasy, it has only a thin veneer of it. Sure, there is a bit of magic thrown around here or there, but if not for the strange names and “sorcery,” it is a contemporary story about a mafia hitman.<br /><br />I read somewhere (I believe it was Ursula K. Le Guin’s book on writing) that in order for a novel to be a “fantasy” she felt it should have such a “fantastical” feel that a reader knew this could not take place down the street. Le Guin even gave an example of this, using an excerpt from a popular 80s fantasy novel. She quoted an entire passage from said “fantasy,” changed the kings to senators, holy priests to representatives and illustrated how this “fantasy” work read like a story about Washington, D.C.. I’m going to try to do the same, but I’m no Le Guin so bear with me. <br /><br />	<i>We ate the meal in silence, enjoying each other’s company, feeling no need to talk. As we were finishing, Cathy said, “So, you get work, while I stay home and wither away from boredom.”<br />	“You don’t look withered to me,” I said, checking. “And I don’t remember your asking me for help with that little matter last month.”<br />	“Hmmmmph,” she said. “I didn’t need any help with that, but this looks like something big. I recognized the target. I hope you are getting a reasonable price for him.”<br />	I told her what I was getting for him.<br />	She raised her eyebrows. “Nice! Who wants him?”<br />	I looked around the restaurant, which was almost deserted. I didn’t like taking chances, but Cathy deserved an answer. “The whole bloody Gambino family wants him, or will if and when they find out.”<br />	“What did he do?” She asked. “He didn’t start talking, did he?”<br />	I shuddered. “No, not that, thank the Virgin Mary. He ran off with nine million dollars in family operating funds.”</i><br />	<br />I changed only 5 words in that passage. Now, instead of Vlad Taltos the human assassin in an elvish empire, we have Vlad the local hitman, trying to take down a mob boss who has taken off with the family’s cash. And this is only one example and can basically be done throughout the whole book. Naturally, some spots take more than 5 words to transform the story, but you see the point.<br /><br />This sort of thing doesn’t bother some people. If that is you, so be it. But if I wanted to read a novel about the mafia, I’d rather do so without the strange names and sorcery thrown in. Like I said however, it is a personal choice.<br /><br /><b>2)</b> <i>Jhereg</i> is written in first-person narrative by the author. Nothing wrong with that in and of itself (Mark Lawrence pulled this off brilliantly in <i>Prince of Thorns</i>), but it does not seem to work here after a while. Quickly, Vlad’s constant descriptions of his actions like <i>“I had my back to the door”</i> or <i>“I approached slowly, sizing him up, reaching for my daggers even though my palms were slick with sweat”</i> began to read like a shopping list. It did not sound natural, and it really limited what I actually saw in the fight scenes, making me feel disconnected with everything else that was going on. Nope, instead of actually reading about Aliera doing something awesome, I have to wait for someone to describe it to Vlad. <br /><br />Also, I felt that the first-person narrative made the scene transitions awkward throughout the book and slowed down the general pacing of the story.<br /><br />Perhaps these complaints are merely personal preference, but as I alluded to, I've read other books that pulled off first-person narrative without making me complain. Maybe it is just me, but it seems that Brust doesn't do as good of a job with it as other authors - at least in this book.<br /><br /><b>3)</b> No romance of any kind. I mean, even though Vlad and Cawti are married, they act like business acquaintances. Sure, they talk about work or make dinner for one another, but other than that sort of “friendly” type of relationship, nothing is going on here. Now, I know that might not bother some of you, but I mean relationships, sex, and all that sort of thing is part of normal human existence. The fact that it was totally ignored for the whole mafia hitman thing really struck me as odd. <br /><br />Yet again, maybe it’s a personal preference. But I thought I’d mention it for those of you who like to see some romance or some hot sex, because you are not going to see either in Jhereg. And before anyone mentions it, I know this was written in the 80s, but my God, Tolkien wrote more smoldering, sexual tension in LoTR than Brust does here.<br /><br /><b>4)</b> Lastly, if you are one of those people that loves reading about some grand, new world and its magic or history (What we now label world building) Jhereg is going to disappoint you: the world building is at the bare minimum. Brust only includes the details necessary to remind you this is not happening in New York City and Vlad is not really a hitman, but an assassin in another world. Sure, we have weapons that destroy souls and talk about ancient Dragaeran Houses or the Orb, but they are fleeting, can easily be omitted without impacting the “hitman” plot and leaves one intrigued, but unsatisfied, with his/her knowledge about the “world” Vlad exists in.<br /><br />To sum up, <i>Jhereg</i> is a decent book. It is entertaining and quickly read, which is why I gave it a 2 star rating. When I was a teenager, I loved the book and would have rated it 3.5 or 4 stars. Unfortunately, some things do not age “well,” and this book is one of those things in my opinion. It just pales in comparison to the type of fantasy novels we have all grown accustom to these days. But if you are needing to waste a couple of hours and don’t want to read another “detective” novel, pick this one up. It might make you *YAWN* in its simplicity, but it probably will keep you awake long enough to finish it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1312713300437525759" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6161505460768091702"><b>Ehr. Mah. Gerd. </b><br/><br/>Vlad Taltos. Oh what’s that? Is that a badass name for a badass main character? Why yes, yes it is. Look at that name. <i>Look at it.</i> It fits him perfectly. Clear. Concise. <b>
  <i>Ominous</i>
</b>. <br/><br/>You know your MC is a badass when he’s in the middle of an internal monologue and subtly lets slip that he’s been <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[
  <b>killed and resurrected</b>
 <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> before and then just keeps on talking like it’s no big deal. I was all “La-la-la, this story is neato!” but then "Wait. Wut?” I h</span>
  <span id="freeText6161505460768091702" style="display:none"><b>Ehr. Mah. Gerd. </b><br><br>Vlad Taltos. Oh what’s that? Is that a badass name for a badass main character? Why yes, yes it is. Look at that name. <i>Look at it.</i> It fits him perfectly. Clear. Concise. <b>
  <i>Ominous</i>
</b>. <br><br>You know your MC is a badass when he’s in the middle of an internal monologue and subtly lets slip that he’s been <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  <b>killed and resurrected</b>
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> before and then just keeps on talking like it’s no big deal. I was all “La-la-la, this story is neato!” but then "Wait. Wut?” I had to go back and read it again before demanding that someone shut the front door. <br><br>And it just keeps going like that. Right when you think that you can settle down and relax for a frigging minute he tells you how he met his wife. You know how people meet, fall in love and then wind up wanting to kill each other? Yeah, that…but backwards. <br><br>His wife is just one of many badass females in this story. There’s also a dragon, a master thief and…Sethra. I have no idea what she is. Actually, she sort of skeeves me out. Undead dragon? Necromatic nightmare? I dunno. Either way, I don’t recommend messing with her. <br><br>So here’s where I would normally go into detail about the plot and the world building and blah, blah, blah and I just <i>tried</i> to do that and not only can I not do it without confusing the hell out of all of you *cough* and myself *cough* but I don’t <i>want</i> to put it in here because I just…can’t. It’s too good and there’s no way in hell I’ll do it justice. Just know that the worldbuilding is strong without ever feeling like an info-dump, the descriptions of magic are detailed without ever being overwhelming and the plot is superb. I couldn’t even guess at the next twist because I. Never. Saw. Them. Coming. <br><br><b>HOW REFRESHING</b><br><br>Okay so what else? I suppose I should tell you not to go into this thinking High Fantasy. There isn’t paragraph after paragraph devoted to the painting of epic scenery, there aren’t highly detailed descriptions of clothing or customs, this is more of a head game. Most of the book is devoted to our MC and his support cast trying to figure out just what the hell is going on. <br><br>I’ll leave you with an example of why I had so much damn fun while reading this. You see, not only is the MC a badass but he has this dry sense of humor that pervades every single page. I pretty much had a shit eating grin on my face from the beginning to the end, so if you like some fantasy mixed with a good mystery and served up with a side of snark, then I urge you to try <i>Jhereg</i>. You won’t regret it. <br><br><i>“She smiled at me. We were all friends here. Morrolan carried Blackwand, which slew a thousand at the Wall of Barrit’s Tomb. Aliera carried Pathfinder, which they say served a power higher than the Empire. Sethra carried Iceflame, which embodied within it the power of the Dzur Mountain. I carried myself rather well, thank you.”</i><br><br><b>Buddy read with Anne and Kathie!</b><br><br><a href="http://litchickhitlist.blogspot.com/2013/07/jhereg-by-steven-brust.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380236610i/681458._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">

<div id="review_279085667" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/279085667" />
    <a title="carol. " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3978225-carol"><img alt="carol. " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1307934801p2/3978225.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/279085667?book_show_action=true">Feb 16, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="carol. " class="user" itemprop="url" name="carol. " href="/user/show/3978225-carol">carol. </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780441385515" href="/book/show/1410207.Jhereg">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fantasy fans</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=male-lead">male-lead</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer279085667" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10854048505298387917">The recent release of <i>Iorich</i> sent me down the path of re-reading the Taltos series. While Iorich was enjoyable and engrossing, memories sent me back to the inaugural Vlad. Sophisticated writing, interesting characters and one seriously convoluted plot. It's interesting, because this is the fourth book in the timeline of the series and Vlad's history, but actually the first published (echoes of Lucas). I'd recommend reading <i>Jhereg</i> first, as it's told in a largely linear fashion with only a few fl</span>
  <span id="freeText10854048505298387917" style="display:none">The recent release of <i>Iorich</i> sent me down the path of re-reading the Taltos series. While Iorich was enjoyable and engrossing, memories sent me back to the inaugural Vlad. Sophisticated writing, interesting characters and one seriously convoluted plot. It's interesting, because this is the fourth book in the timeline of the series and Vlad's history, but actually the first published (echoes of Lucas). I'd recommend reading <i>Jhereg</i> first, as it's told in a largely linear fashion with only a few flashbacks, and as such is a decent introduction to the world's political and social structure. As the series continues, Brust starts playing in interesting ways with narrative, so it helps to already have a solid grip on the basics. <br /><br />Characters are done well, with broad brushstrokes. We get some of Vlad's early years, and we are given the background on his initial connection with Loiosh. His friendships with Dragons Morrolan and Aliera, and his lieutenant Krager are well established in this book, with nice repartee and camaraderie. Loiosh is a smart sidekick, but not overly humanized. The plot is entirely plausible within the world setting, and although Vlad's antagonist has spent decades planning his revenge, his rationale is somewhat understandable and brings a sense of sympathy even as Vlad works to save the situation.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10854048505298387917" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_119216086" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/119216086" />
    <a title="Brad" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1022982-brad"><img alt="Brad" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442484575p2/1022982.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/119216086?book_show_action=true">Aug 29, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brad" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brad" href="/user/show/1022982-brad">Brad</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780441385539" href="/book/show/1410206.Jhereg">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Amber</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Brad by: </span>
      Sherri Murphy-Jacobs &amp; D.
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=fantasy-urban-fantasy">fantasy-urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer119216086" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5689566303971428259"><i>Immediate Reaction:</i> This was a blast. A little fantasy-noir fun for anyone who likes bad men behaving with honour. Vlad Taltos is an anti-hero extraordinaire, and all the minor characters and relationships he's surrounded with are equally cool.<br/><br/><i>Later:</i> This is only the second book I've read by <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/27704.Steven_Brust' title='Steven Brust' rel='nofollow noopener'>Steven Brust</a>, and the first I've read that he wrote alone. I read his collaboration with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/22548.Emma_Bull' title='Emma Bull' rel='nofollow noopener'>Emma Bull</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/140149.Freedom_and_Necessity' title='Freedom and Necessity by Steven Brust' rel='nofollow noopener'>Freedom and Necessity</a> a couple of months ago, and loved their book so much I knew I had to hunt down their </span>
  <span id="freeText5689566303971428259" style="display:none"><i>Immediate Reaction:</i> This was a blast. A little fantasy-noir fun for anyone who likes bad men behaving with honour. Vlad Taltos is an anti-hero extraordinaire, and all the minor characters and relationships he's surrounded with are equally cool.<br /><br /><i>Later:</i> This is only the second book I've read by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/27704.Steven_Brust" title="Steven Brust" rel="nofollow noopener">Steven Brust</a>, and the first I've read that he wrote alone. I read his collaboration with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/22548.Emma_Bull" title="Emma Bull" rel="nofollow noopener">Emma Bull</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/140149.Freedom_and_Necessity" title="Freedom and Necessity by Steven Brust" rel="nofollow noopener">Freedom and Necessity</a> a couple of months ago, and loved their book so much I knew I had to hunt down their other works and give them a go. What <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/133454.Jhereg__Vlad_Taltos___1_" title="Jhereg (Vlad Taltos, #1) by Steven Brust" rel="nofollow noopener">Jhereg</a> delivered was totally unexpected.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/140149.Freedom_and_Necessity" title="Freedom and Necessity by Steven Brust" rel="nofollow noopener">F and N</a> was a beautiful literary work that obviously suffers in its readership by being written by a pair of Sci-Fi/Fantasy authors. And I expected more of the same with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/133454.Jhereg__Vlad_Taltos___1_" title="Jhereg (Vlad Taltos, #1) by Steven Brust" rel="nofollow noopener">Jhereg</a>. But there is little "literary" in the first of the Vlad Taltos books, but that doesn't make it any less readable. In fact, it might actually make it much more of an addiction inducing habit. <br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/133454.Jhereg__Vlad_Taltos___1_" title="Jhereg (Vlad Taltos, #1) by Steven Brust" rel="nofollow noopener">Jhereg</a> is a bit like a fantasy detective story, or a "fantasy noir" (as I called it earlier), with assassin/crime boss/information collector Vlad Taltos taking the role of obligatory hardbitte detective from the works of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/16927.Dashiell_Hammett" title="Dashiell Hammett" rel="nofollow noopener">Dashiel Hammett</a> or <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/50948.Mickey_Spillane" title="Mickey Spillane" rel="nofollow noopener">Mickey Spillane</a>. And it's as good as the former and better than the latter. <br /><br />Vlad is surrounded by an original and exotic fantasy world, killer allies (his pseudo-cousin Aliera is a personal favourite), a smart ass familiar named Loiosh, a seamy underworld, nasty enemies (including one who calls himself "Demon"), witchcraft and sorcery (which are nothing alike), genetic engineering (for the slightest touch of Sci-Fi) and the most mundane of domestic lives. Even better, he is one of the most likable antiheroes in all of Fantasy.<br /><br />I understand from some of my goodreads friends that the depth of this series -- as it goes on, and it goes on for a long time -- is impressive. I've already started <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/817357.Yendi__Vlad_Taltos___2_" title="Yendi (Vlad Taltos, #2) by Steven Brust" rel="nofollow noopener">Yendi</a>, so it's a good bet that I am going to experience this depth first hand. Having read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/140149.Freedom_and_Necessity" title="Freedom and Necessity by Steven Brust" rel="nofollow noopener">F and N</a>, I believe that depth is possible. Now I just need to track down <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/70582.War_for_the_Oaks" title="War for the Oaks by Emma Bull" rel="nofollow noopener">War for the Oaks</a>, so I can experience how the other half of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/140149.Freedom_and_Necessity" title="Freedom and Necessity by Steven Brust" rel="nofollow noopener">F and N</a> writes when out of collaboration.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5689566303971428259" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_3156284943" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3156284943" />
    <a title="Dirk Grobbelaar" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3102740-dirk-grobbelaar"><img alt="Dirk Grobbelaar" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1545117991p2/3102740.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3156284943?book_show_action=true">Jan 30, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dirk Grobbelaar" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dirk Grobbelaar" href="/user/show/3102740-dirk-grobbelaar">Dirk Grobbelaar</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780441385546" href="/book/show/1281575.Jhereg">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3102740-dirk-grobbelaar?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3102740-dirk-grobbelaar?shelf=books-i-own-in-omnibus-format">books-i-own-in-omnibus-format</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3156284943" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17357756284754714824">I’m not typically fond of stories relying heavily on “rogue” class characters, such as thieves or assassins. These tales tend to be urban, i.e. confined to cities and towns. I, myself, prefer a more holistic approach to fantasy worlds in storytelling, because I tend to visualize a lot. <br/><br/>However, this book drew me in nicely. The world is actually presented by the author with a remarkable amount of confidence, given the lack of exposition / history. Information is provided piecemeal and in a matter</span>
  <span id="freeText17357756284754714824" style="display:none">I’m not typically fond of stories relying heavily on “rogue” class characters, such as thieves or assassins. These tales tend to be urban, i.e. confined to cities and towns. I, myself, prefer a more holistic approach to fantasy worlds in storytelling, because I tend to visualize a lot. <br /><br />However, this book drew me in nicely. The world is actually presented by the author with a remarkable amount of confidence, given the lack of exposition / history. Information is provided piecemeal and in a matter-of-fact fashion. Some of these tidbits are truly tantalizing, and piqued my interest greatly. What is the enclouding? Is the empire really more than 1000 centuries old? Who is The Necromancer? What is the Imperial Orb… and the Greater Sea of Chaos? Who were the Jenoine? And the Serioli? Etc etc. Some of these questions are eventually (and fortunately) answered as the book progresses, but some aren’t. As such, while the world has a very established feel, some aspects are left to the imagination.<br /><br /><i>"There is no substitute for good manners - except fast reflexes."</i><br /><br />The novel deals with one Vlad Taltos, an assassin of note, who accepts a contract that isn’t quite what it seems. That, by the way, is one hell of an understatement. <br />Did he bite off more than he could chew? Intrigue ensues as the protagonist sets off to negotiate the quagmire of Dragaerian Empire and Noble House politics, before he can get down to the task at hand.<br /><br />Vlad Taltos is an interesting character though. He may not be all he appears to be, and he has a Jhereg familiar, which is basically a venomous pet dragon of diminutive size. He also surrounds himself with some gnarly, if somewhat unpredictable, folk. This is important in the larger scheme of things since Vlad Taltos is a human, and humans are at the bottom of the food chain. <br /><br /><i>I found myself filled with awe at the magnificence of [his] plan. It was tremendous!</i><br /><br />At the time Jhereg was published, it was the first book in the Vlad Taltos series (it has subsequently been ousted, chronologically speaking) and as such there are no previous events that laid the groundwork for the world depicted here, and yet it feels like a setting fully fleshed. I particularly enjoyed the clear distinction between sorcery and witchcraft (which is, arguably, comparable to the differences between divine magic and arcane magic) and the study of genetics as it pertains to the narrative.<br /><br />It’s also important to note the impact of <b>time</b> on the story at large. The Dragaerans are very, <b>very</b> long lived, and the author cleverly exploits this to affect the intrigue (as it should). Events that appear fairly innocuous on the face of it are unraveled to reveal complexities and intricacies initially unimagined, and spanning several human lifetimes. <br /><br />Which brings me to one perceived shortcoming of the story: while some plot events are dazzling, others are fairly simplistic and, well, fall flat. I suppose I could put this down to first novel syndrome? <br /><br /><i>"True heroics must be carefully planned - and strenuously avoided."</i><br /><br />I am a sucker for floating castles, demonic weapons, sorcery, teleporting assassins and little dragons. I went into this not wanting metaphor or analogy. Sometimes I crave the ridiculous and the fantastical. This book scratched that itch and read pretty quick as well. Double whammy.<br /><br /><i>“And, of course, we had the Necromancer standing by, just in case there were problems."</i> </span>
  <a data-text-id="17357756284754714824" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Mimi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2490110-mimi"><img alt="Mimi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1424631975p2/2490110.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/687542258?book_show_action=true">Aug 06, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780441385546" href="/book/show/1281575.Jhereg">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2490110-mimi?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2490110-mimi?shelf=dragons">dragons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2490110-mimi?shelf=2017">2017</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2490110-mimi?shelf=high-fantasy">high-fantasy</a>,

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer687542258" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6632489565038192682">Satisfyingly good. The kind of good that makes you anxious to get to the next book. The kind of good that makes you glad there are over ten books in the series. The kind of good that makes <i>me</i> not care about book orders. Maybe it's a good thing these books are written out of order?--is a thing I never thought I'd say. But I have a good feeling about Steven Brust and I trust he'll deliver. <br/><br/>It's been awhile since high fantasy has been this good for me, and it's been even longer since I liked a POV </span>
  <span id="freeText6632489565038192682" style="display:none">Satisfyingly good. The kind of good that makes you anxious to get to the next book. The kind of good that makes you glad there are over ten books in the series. The kind of good that makes <i>me</i> not care about book orders. Maybe it's a good thing these books are written out of order?--is a thing I never thought I'd say. But I have a good feeling about Steven Brust and I trust he'll deliver. <br /><br />It's been awhile since high fantasy has been this good for me, and it's been even longer since I liked a POV main character in high fantasy enough to know that I'll like whatever trials and tribulations he's put through. And I like Vlad Taltos. Thus far, he's already shown himself to be a multifaceted character full of nuance, and I can only imagine he'll get more complex with each book.<br /><br />Plus, there are dragons everywhere.<br /><br />Full review to come... when I get through the series.<br /><br />* * * * *<br /><br />Trying to figure out the order of this series is giving me a serious case of involuntary twitching. So far from what I've gleaned on various forums and reviews, the publication order is completely different from the chronological order.<br /><br /><i>*more twitching*</i><br /><br />But the order in which you read these books does not matter. At all. Because they were purposely written out of order.<br /><br /><i>*bangs head on desk*</i><br /><br />Why.<br /><br />(I have a thing for publication order)<br /><br />* * * * *<br /><br />Publication order goes like this:<br /><b>Jhereg</b><br />Yendi<br />Teckla<br />Taltos<br />Phoenix<br />Athyra<br />Orca<br />Dragon<br />Issola<br />Dzur<br />Jhegaala<br />Iorich<br />Tiassa<br />Hawk<br /><br />But chronological order goes like this:<br />Taltos<br />Dragon<br />Yendi<br /><b>Jhereg</b><br />Teckla<br />Phoenix<br />Jhegaala<br />Athyra<br />Orca<br />Issola<br />Dzur<br />Iorich<br />Tiassa<br />Hawk<br /><br />The only book I have is Jhereg, so I'm gonna start there.<br /><br />Cross-posted at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://covers2covers.wordpress.com/2017/05/03/jhereg-vlad-taltos-1-by-steven-brust/">https://covers2covers.wordpress.com/2...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="6632489565038192682" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1309986521" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1309986521" />
    <a title="Bradley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4213258-bradley"><img alt="Bradley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508811508p2/4213258.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1309986521?book_show_action=true">Jun 16, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bradley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bradley" href="/user/show/4213258-bradley">Bradley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780441385546" href="/book/show/1281575.Jhereg">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=worldbuilding-sf">worldbuilding-sf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1309986521" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12612842658208959437">While there was nothing absolutely mind-blowing about the plot or the fantasy, the one thing that really stood out in this book was the fantastic writing.<br/><br/>It was absolutely some of the easiest reading I've had for an obviously detailed and fleshed out world full of lots of magic, interesting races, very long lived people, and dragons. It flew by so quickly and easily, I was rather surprised at how much info-dump never came across as info-dump. I learned so much about the world, naturally, that I </span>
  <span id="freeText12612842658208959437" style="display:none">While there was nothing absolutely mind-blowing about the plot or the fantasy, the one thing that really stood out in this book was the fantastic writing.<br /><br />It was absolutely some of the easiest reading I've had for an obviously detailed and fleshed out world full of lots of magic, interesting races, very long lived people, and dragons. It flew by so quickly and easily, I was rather surprised at how much info-dump never came across as info-dump. I learned so much about the world, naturally, that I was giddy after the reading.<br /><br />Is it because I've grown very used to the tropes involved, over so many years of enjoying fantasy? Possibly. But then, that's another reason I need to give this book props. From the mid-eighties, it still comes off as hugely superior in execution, characterization, big ideas, and joy. This is SUPERIOR fantasy.<br /><br />I've read my fair share of SUPERIOR fantasy, of course, but this one feels so effortless.<br /><br />Assassins? Check. Dragons? Check. Near immortals everywhere you look? Check. Tons and tons of magic? Absolutely.<br /><br />I'm pretty sure I'm going to fly through all Brust's novels in no time whatsoever. They're pretty damn fantastic and smart.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12612842658208959437" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

As good as all that is, it is the main character of Vlad Taltos (assassin, witch and rogue) and his "jhereg" familiar that make the series so special. Highly recommended. <br/> </span>

    <a title="Sebastien Castell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4846758-sebastien-castell"><img alt="Sebastien Castell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1378071485p2/4846758.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/182381102?book_show_action=true">Jul 06, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sebastien Castell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sebastien Castell" href="/user/show/4846758-sebastien-castell">Sebastien Castell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4846758-sebastien-castell?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer182381102" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5682310804760033465">This is the third in my list of books that inspired me to start writing fantasy and in many ways is the most influential. The hero of the series, Vlad Taltos, is an assassin, which is, you know, not an especially nice thing to be. The thing is, deep down Vlad really wants to be a nice guy. He just needs to kill a few shitbags first. Now it's true that the list of people Vlad needs to kill includes pretty much the entire Dragaeran Empire, but he's willing to leave a few off the list if they chang</span>
  <span id="freeText5682310804760033465" style="display:none">This is the third in my list of books that inspired me to start writing fantasy and in many ways is the most influential. The hero of the series, Vlad Taltos, is an assassin, which is, you know, not an especially nice thing to be. The thing is, deep down Vlad really wants to be a nice guy. He just needs to kill a few shitbags first. Now it's true that the list of people Vlad needs to kill includes pretty much the entire Dragaeran Empire, but he's willing to leave a few off the list if they change their ways. Oh, and Vlad's sidekick a wise-talking miniature dragon who calls him 'Boss' all the time. Seriously - who wouldn't want to read that?<br /><br />Brust blends heroic fantasy with a film noir, almost Raymond Chandler-esque voice. In fact, <i>Jhereg</i> was the book that taught me you could write fantasy without having your characters talk in fake British accents and spouting thee's and thou's every sentence. It's a short book by today's standards, and one that will fly by. Fortunately, there's a dozen more to keep you busy once you're done. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5682310804760033465" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6306030634810969341">Reread Feb2012, review added. <br/><br/>I originally gave this 4 stars, although I've read it numerous times & really enjoyed it. I just never thought it had any redeeming features beyond sheer enjoyment. Now that I've read most of the rest of the series, I see on a re-read that the craftsmanship of this story demands another star. <br/><br/>This is not the first book in the chronology of the series, but it is the first published. Why should you read it first? Because the author couldn't have picked a better way to</span>
  <span id="freeText6306030634810969341" style="display:none">Reread Feb2012, review added. <br /><br />I originally gave this 4 stars, although I've read it numerous times &amp; really enjoyed it. I just never thought it had any redeeming features beyond sheer enjoyment. Now that I've read most of the rest of the series, I see on a re-read that the craftsmanship of this story demands another star. <br /><br />This is not the first book in the chronology of the series, but it is the first published. Why should you read it first? Because the author couldn't have picked a better way to introduce the reader to an entirely new world &amp; mythology. The story demands our likable anti-hero, Vlad Taltos, look deeply into another character. His search uncovers more than expected &amp; gives us an understanding of the world that we never would have had otherwise. Not only is it entirely entertaining &amp; fast moving, but I had no trouble at all remembering odd names &amp; characters. Each comes alive in a way that sticks in the memory, with a depth that is incredible for the terse wording. Not just the main characters either, although there were most of a dozen of those alone. It's truly an amazing feat.<br /><br />Now I REALLY want to go on to the next book, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/817357.Yendi__Vlad_Taltos___2_" title="Yendi (Vlad Taltos, #2) by Steven Brust" rel="nofollow noopener">Yendi</a>, but I have other commitments - damn!</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chris " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chris " href="/user/show/1956959-chris">Chris </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780441385546" href="/book/show/1281575.Jhereg">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1956959-chris?shelf=read-owned-paperback">read-owned-paperback</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer69983947" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1613189843262605145">This was a delightful beginning to a series that I am sure to be addicted to very soon. In fact, I've already jumped into the second volume.<br/><br/>But on this. Jhereg is a first person narrative of an assassin and a particular job he undertook. A huge amount of money offered showed that if something seemed too good to be true, it probably was.<br/><br/>Mischief and mayhem ensue. What I thought of as a combination of a crime caper and an epic fantasy turned out to be a quickly paced and often humorous adventure. </span>
  <span id="freeText1613189843262605145" style="display:none">This was a delightful beginning to a series that I am sure to be addicted to very soon. In fact, I've already jumped into the second volume.<br /><br />But on this. Jhereg is a first person narrative of an assassin and a particular job he undertook. A huge amount of money offered showed that if something seemed too good to be true, it probably was.<br /><br />Mischief and mayhem ensue. What I thought of as a combination of a crime caper and an epic fantasy turned out to be a quickly paced and often humorous adventure. Vlad Taltos has a familiar which happens to be a jhereg, a miniature dragon-like creature. And, no surprise with Brust characters, Loiosh is quite the smartass. Witty banter between familiar and master, along with a great cast of hirelings and allies makes this a book to keep the reader guessing, on the edge of his/her seat, and occasionally laughing.<br /><br />The fight scenes were great, I wasn't surprised to later read that Brust took lessons in fencing, as he was able to describe the swordfights in quite a vivid manner. Add a touch of The Three Musketeers to that adventure/heist/fantasy description.<br /><br />On to more Vlad adventures!</span>
  <a data-text-id="1613189843262605145" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_27319105" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/27319105" />
    <a title="Melissa McShane" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1329059-melissa-mcshane"><img alt="Melissa McShane" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1216147749p2/1329059.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/27319105?book_show_action=true">Jul 15, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melissa McShane" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melissa McShane" href="/user/show/1329059-melissa-mcshane">Melissa McShane</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780441385546" href="/book/show/1281575.Jhereg">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1329059-melissa-mcshane?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1329059-melissa-mcshane?shelf=sword-and-sorcery">sword-and-sorcery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1329059-melissa-mcshane?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1329059-melissa-mcshane?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer27319105" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16471729660490080951">Re-read 9/18/17, as audiobook. The year I was thirteen, I read and re-read obsessively the same, perhaps, thirty books. Keep in mind I had almost nothing but free time and I read three to four books a day. That is a lot of times to re-read anything. I've since learned that this is not an uncommon phenomenon among children and young teens, and it does not indicate any problems with their overall reading habit. For me, it was a matter of falling into comfortable grooves, revisiting powerful experi</span>
  <span id="freeText16471729660490080951" style="display:none">Re-read 9/18/17, as audiobook. The year I was thirteen, I read and re-read obsessively the same, perhaps, thirty books. Keep in mind I had almost nothing but free time and I read three to four books a day. That is a lot of times to re-read anything. I've since learned that this is not an uncommon phenomenon among children and young teens, and it does not indicate any problems with their overall reading habit. For me, it was a matter of falling into comfortable grooves, revisiting powerful experiences, like going to a restaurant and repeatedly ordering some signature dish even when other foods are available. Yes, there are good foods, and yes, someday you'll try them, but why not eat the thing that you love best, particularly when it is perfectly prepared every time?<br /><br /><i>Jhereg</i> was one of those thirty books. It was recommended to me by a friend who no longer loves fantasy literature, so re-reading it is bittersweet, as it brings back memories of the imaginative worlds we used to build that centered on these masterpieces of fantasy. And <i>Jhereg</i> is definitely one of those. Looking at it from the perspective of far too many years' distance from my thirteen-year-old self, I can see how deceptively simple it is, and yet how skilled Brust was, even that early in his career. The characterization is deftly handled, the worldbuilding is subtle and yet suggests depths he would later plumb in the rest of the series, and Vlad's rage at being human in a world of elves--and at being accepted neither by the humans nor the Dragaerans--is hidden in plain sight. I know I didn't get the complexity of his relationship with his Dragaeran friends; I only saw that they were friends, something that this most recent re-read in internal chronological order makes even more complex.<br /><br />And reading in that order blows my mind. I have no idea how Brust managed to build whole novels around the hints and throwaway lines he tosses out <i>and still keep everything straight</i>. The closest he comes to making a mistake is in the references to the events that eight books later would become <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/27319749" rel="nofollow noopener">Dragon</a>, and even then it's a "mistake" within acceptable parameters for the book he ultimately wrote. Brilliant.<br /><br />Having read it out of order, I was startled when Loiosh didn't sound like Peter Lorre. Apparently the narrator's performance evolved over time, which is nice. Now it's on to <i>Teckla</i>, which I dread.<br /><br />Read 10/6/14: How many times have I read this book? I have no idea. I love Vlad's voice and the world he lives in, and I love all the other characters, especially Loiosh, and the puzzle Vlad has to figure out is both clever and serves as an excellent introduction to Dragaeran society and the Houses that define it. Fun, exciting, and a great beginning to the series (despite not being chronologically the first, but Brust is better than just about anyone at prequels).</span>
  <a data-text-id="16471729660490080951" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1174044719" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1174044719" />
    <a title="Brad" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1022982-brad"><img alt="Brad" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442484575p2/1022982.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1174044719?book_show_action=true">Jan 19, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brad" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brad" href="/user/show/1022982-brad">Brad</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780441385546" href="/book/show/1281575.Jhereg">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=fantasy-urban-fantasy">fantasy-urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=a-floating-bar-of-ivory">a-floating-bar-of-ivory</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=anti-heroes">anti-heroes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=pb-and-j-dipped-in-hot-chocolate">pb-and-j-dipped-in-hot-chocolate</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=fantasy-noir">fantasy-noir</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=remember-sammy-jenkis">remember-sammy-jenkis</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=hollow-calories">hollow-calories</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1174044719" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12492363891672638935">I refuse to look at what I said about this book <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1410206.Jhereg' rel='nofollow noopener'>the last time I read it</a> for fear of influencing what I have to say this time around, but I will certainly do so once I have posted my thoughts.<br/><br/>My thoughts: total bafflement that my second time through <i>Jhereg</i> was like the first time through. The only two things I remembered about the story were Vlad Taltos, our first-person narrating criminal mastermind/assassin and his Lockheed-like dragon, Loiosh. Other than that I didn't remember a thing. It was </span>
  <span id="freeText12492363891672638935" style="display:none">I refuse to look at what I said about this book <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1410206.Jhereg" rel="nofollow noopener">the last time I read it</a> for fear of influencing what I have to say this time around, but I will certainly do so once I have posted my thoughts.<br /><br />My thoughts: total bafflement that my second time through <i>Jhereg</i> was like the first time through. The only two things I remembered about the story were Vlad Taltos, our first-person narrating criminal mastermind/assassin and his Lockheed-like dragon, Loiosh. Other than that I didn't remember a thing. It was like reading it for the first time, and I have to say the experience was a touch off-putting. <br /><br />It is rare for me to reread a book without the entire plot, most of the characterization and even some of the dialogue flooding back, but so little of <i>Jhereg</i> stuck with me that it all felt new. It makes me wonder about the authorial skill of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/27704.Steven_Brust" title="Steven Brust" rel="nofollow noopener">Steven Brust</a>. I have introduced countless friends to his work, specifically his collaboration <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/140149.Freedom_and_Necessity" title="Freedom and Necessity by Steven Brust" rel="nofollow noopener">Freedom and Necessity</a>, but to the Taltos books too, yet I found myself wondering all the way through this if he is as sustaining as a bowl of fried rice at an MSG-laden Chinese Food restaurant. Is he just hollow calories? Perhaps. <br /><br />But I can't help thinking, "Who cares?" I love fried rice at bad Chinese food restaurants. Sure it isn't real Chinese food. It doesn't stick with me. But I fucking love it while I am eating it, and I find myself craving it again and again. The same holds true for me with Vlad Taltos and his machinations in Adrilankha. <br /><br />I am going to go out on a limb here, though, and say something potentially inciting to super-Brust-fans: I get a feeling good old Steve writes his Taltos books as hollow reading calories on purpose. I think he wants us to forget what happened beyond our fondness for the books so we can read them fresh every time. I think his <i>hack-i-ness</i>, for want of a better term, is absolutely intentional. So he isn't an author of hollow calories, but a Chef who knows when to make an airy special for the night in the hopes of packing the booths with bums.<br /><br />Be offended if you like, but keep this in mind: if what I have said is true I love him for it even more than I already did. And if you read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/140149.Freedom_and_Necessity" title="Freedom and Necessity by Steven Brust" rel="nofollow noopener">Freedom and Necessity</a> you'll see where that true love comes from. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12492363891672638935" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer557065816" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1400308323950505440">Via Book Reviews by Niki Hawkes at <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.nikihawkes.com'>www.nikihawkes.com</a><br/><br/>Jhereg was nothing like I thought it would be… it was better! I was expecting a typical “boy gets a dragons and goes out on an epic adventure” book (I guess I need to stop judging by the cover alone). What I ended up with was a cheeky, magical, modern-day assassin mystery that blew my socks off.<br/><br/>Highly interesting characters and plot-lines, it was an extremely fast-paced novel that keeps you page-turning to the very end. And when I say fast-pac</span>
  <span id="freeText1400308323950505440" style="display:none">Via Book Reviews by Niki Hawkes at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.nikihawkes.com">www.nikihawkes.com</a><br /><br />Jhereg was nothing like I thought it would be… it was better! I was expecting a typical “boy gets a dragons and goes out on an epic adventure” book (I guess I need to stop judging by the cover alone). What I ended up with was a cheeky, magical, modern-day assassin mystery that blew my socks off.<br /><br />Highly interesting characters and plot-lines, it was an extremely fast-paced novel that keeps you page-turning to the very end. And when I say fast-paced, I’m not joking around. The author has an incredible “no words wasted” writing style that makes for an exciting read. Trouble is, if you blink or get distracted for even a moment (as I am wont to do) you’ll likely miss something important and plot-advancing – so stay focused!<br /><br />Initially, I thought a draw-back to this series was the lack of attention on setting. I couldn’t tell if the book was taking place in a complete fantasy world or just in a twist of our modern-day (and actually, I’m still not sure). I initially thought the author was lazy, but now I’m starting to suspect he’s a bit brilliant. His overall mastery over other elements of the craft is what clued me in. You see, the story is written in a strong first-person narrative – done well enough that I always felt totally immersed into the character. I now think the reason the reader doesn’t get to see the settings clearer is that the main character doesn’t pay much attention to such commonplace (for him) details. If this is truly the case, the Brust did an excellent job sticking to his chosen perspective, and I applaud him on it.<br /><br />Overall, it was a unique read that I wish I’d picked up years ago. The author has a good fusion of fantasy and mystery that really maintained my attention. Though not the first book chronologically, it is the first book according to the publisher, and that’s good enough for me (especially since the author admitted he has no clue in what order his books should be read).<br /><br />by Niki Hawkes<br /><br />Other books you might like:<br /><br />“Dragon Weather” by Lawrence Watt-Evans<br />“The Thief’s Gamble” by Juliet E. Mckenna<br />“Mistborn” by Brandon Sanderson<br />“Black Sun Rising” by C.S. Friedman<br />“Sword-Dancer” by Jennifer Roberson</span>
