<div id="review_201025498" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/201025498" />
    <a title="Jason" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2613919-jason"><img alt="Jason" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483904179p2/2613919.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/201025498?book_show_action=true">Aug 22, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jason" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jason" href="/user/show/2613919-jason">Jason</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2613919-jason?shelf=read-2011">read-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2613919-jason?shelf=e-books">e-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer201025498" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7994966507366628664">4 Stars<br/><br/>This was a really good beginning to the first book in the Vlad Taltos series. This was my first time reading a Steven Brust novel even though he has been in my queue for as long as I can remember. This is a novel that was first published nearly 30 years ago. It is written in a fashion that keeps it fresh and relative to todays fantasy scene.<br/><br/>The combination of magic(sorcery)and witchcraft is very unique. The book gives some creative back story that explains the difference between the two s</span>
  <span id="freeText7994966507366628664" style="display:none">4 Stars<br /><br />This was a really good beginning to the first book in the Vlad Taltos series. This was my first time reading a Steven Brust novel even though he has been in my queue for as long as I can remember. This is a novel that was first published nearly 30 years ago. It is written in a fashion that keeps it fresh and relative to todays fantasy scene.<br /><br />The combination of magic(sorcery)and witchcraft is very unique. The book gives some creative back story that explains the difference between the two schools of magic. The interaction of the Eastern humans and the western Dragaera(a large reptilian race)adds to the depth of the society and colors our story. Like many current fantasy novels, the Dragaera are organized into different houses, each named after an animal. The Jhereg house, the house of the mongrels is named after the snake like serpent called the Jhereg.<br /><br />Our protagonist name is Vladamir Taltos. He is a human that belongs to the Dragaera house of Jhereg because his father bought them their title with all of his earnings.<br /><br />Vlad is very likable and his diverse background of being raised in the west in the house Jhereg, while also being trained in the Eastern ways by his grandfather, make him a formidable force. Vlad is an assassin, plain and simple...Does that make him a bad guy...well.<br /><br />Vlad practices his witchcraft and has a jhereg familiar named Looish. They communicate with each other telepathically. There is a lot of humor and clever banter between the two. Their relationship is really a center piece that make this book special.<br /><br />This short story in the end, is a story about revenge. There is a mystery to unravel, and the sides are not always clear. It takes a while for the pieces of the story to come together, but when they do the payoff is great.<br /><br />I really enjoyed this first book and now am a fan of Steven Brust...Bring on more Vlad... Highly recommended.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7994966507366628664" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_623901790" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/623901790" />
    <a title="Mogsy (MMOGC)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4379514-mogsy-mmogc"><img alt="Mogsy (MMOGC)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1286325553p2/4379514.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/623901790?book_show_action=true">May 24, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mogsy (MMOGC)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mogsy (MMOGC)" href="/user/show/4379514-mogsy-mmogc">Mogsy (MMOGC)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780441385546" href="/book/show/1281575.Jhereg">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4379514-mogsy-mmogc?shelf=epic">epic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4379514-mogsy-mmogc?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4379514-mogsy-mmogc?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4379514-mogsy-mmogc?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4379514-mogsy-mmogc?shelf=assassins">assassins</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer623901790" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1799772988308418182">Guess this is what you'd call an oldie but a goodie. I can't believe I hadn't heard of Steven Brust until a few weeks ago, but he was recommended to me by a gaming friend of mine, and then another good friend jumped into the Twitter conversation to second the recommendation. So, that's two shoutouts from a couple of people whose opinions I highly value, and that's when I knew I had to get my hands on this book, posthaste!<br/><br/>Jhereg is the beginning of a whole bunch of books set in Brust's Dragaera w</span>
  <span id="freeText1799772988308418182" style="display:none">Guess this is what you'd call an oldie but a goodie. I can't believe I hadn't heard of Steven Brust until a few weeks ago, but he was recommended to me by a gaming friend of mine, and then another good friend jumped into the Twitter conversation to second the recommendation. So, that's two shoutouts from a couple of people whose opinions I highly value, and that's when I knew I had to get my hands on this book, posthaste!<br /><br />Jhereg is the beginning of a whole bunch of books set in Brust's Dragaera world. It is the first novel to be published in the Vlad Taltos series, even though its place is actually fourth or so in its timeline. It introduces us to Vladimir Taltos, an Easterner (human) working as a killer-for-hire in the House of Jhereg in a setting where his kind are barely tolerated by a race of long-lived, statuesque sorcerers called the Dragaerans (or, as my friend told me, just think of them as "elves"!) Being a Jhereg doesn't help either, since their faction is like the mafia of the Dragaeran world.<br /><br />One day, a powerful Jhereg boss offers Vlad a lucrative contract to track down and assassinate a council member who stole millions of gold from the house. It is discovered, unfortunately, that this thief has fled to Castle Black, home of the Dragonlord Morrolan who is also Vlad's good friend. Now Vlad has to try and figure out a way to fulfill his contract without royally pissing off Morrolan, whose strict rule against the killing of anyone on his premises while they are under his protection is proving to be more than just a minor inconvenience.<br /><br />At just 200-something pages, this was a very quick read. Despite the volume's relative thinness, however, there is a lot information crammed in here. You'll immediately get the sense of hugeness from the world of Dragaera, and I admit I spent much of the first half of this book feeling like I was missing something, because not everything about the setting is explained right away. There will be names of people, animals, factions, cultural traditions, events in history, etc. that are alluded to, but won't mean anything to you until you get further into the book (or even the series). Even now, I wish I had more room in this review to give examples of all the strange magical spells, weapons, creatures, lore and customs that are in this book, but there's just too damn much. The good news is, everything you need know in order to understand and follow the story will be there, and it will come in time.<br /><br />I also really liked the writing style, the fast pace and the lightness of it. Normally when you get high fantasy featuring a world full of magic and so much history, along with noble sorcerers and lords and ladies and such and such, you'd expect the writing style and dialogue to be somewhat serious and austere. Not so much with this book, which includes instances of modern day habits or colloquialisms, and that played a part in making Jhereg easy to get into and reading it so much fun.<br /><br />It's got a great story overall, involving a plot about an assassination, but which almost reads more like story about a heist. It has elements of mystery in it too, as Vlad likes to conduct investigations and figure out the solutions from the clues he finds. He as much as admits that he prefers the process of planning an assassination to the actual assassinating, and events in the story reflect that. It just struck me as interesting especially when compared to more recent fantasy novels about assassins, which tend to be darker and more action-oriented, and Jhereg was published before I was even born.<br /><br />The series is still going on today, with book 14 expected to come out later this year. So glad I discovered these books, thanks to my friends. I've got a lot of books in my to-be-read pile, but since all the Vlad novels seem to be such quick reads, there might actually be hope of me finishing up to Tiassa before Hawk comes out. Maybe.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1799772988308418182" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_186566008" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/186566008" />
    <a title="Kat  Hooper" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2177891-kat-hooper"><img alt="Kat  Hooper" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1533675060p2/2177891.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/186566008?book_show_action=true">Jul 19, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kat  Hooper" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kat  Hooper" href="/user/show/2177891-kat-hooper">Kat  Hooper</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780441385546" href="/book/show/1281575.Jhereg">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2177891-kat-hooper?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer186566008" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11516950933393316701">3.5 s stars<br/>Originally posted (with links) at FanLit.<br/><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.fantasyliterature.com/reviews/jhereg/'>http://www.fantasyliterature.com/revi...</a><br/><br/>Audio readers, rejoice! Finally, Steven Brust’s VLAD TALTOS novels have been produced in audio by Audible Frontiers. For years I’ve been planning to read this long series and have only been waiting for this moment.<br/><br/>The VLAD TALTOS novels follow Vlad Taltos, a well-known and highly successful human assassin living on the planet Dragaera. The native species, the Dragaerans, are a tall long-lived race created</span>
  <span id="freeText11516950933393316701" style="display:none">3.5 s stars<br />Originally posted (with links) at FanLit.<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.fantasyliterature.com/reviews/jhereg/">http://www.fantasyliterature.com/revi...</a><br /><br />Audio readers, rejoice! Finally, Steven Brust’s VLAD TALTOS novels have been produced in audio by Audible Frontiers. For years I’ve been planning to read this long series and have only been waiting for this moment.<br /><br />The VLAD TALTOS novels follow Vlad Taltos, a well-known and highly successful human assassin living on the planet Dragaera. The native species, the Dragaerans, are a tall long-lived race created by sorcerers who cross-bred humans and certain animals. The characteristics of the animals give each clan, or “House,” its name, physical features, and personality traits. The exception is the house of Jhereg (named after a small dragon-like creature) which is a low-class conglomerate of outcasts from other clans and also any true humans who can buy their way in, which is what Vlad Taltos’ father did. Each of Brusts’ novels in this series is named after one of the Dragaeran houses.<br /><br />In this first installment, Jhereg, we meet Vlad Taltos and his familiar, Loiosh, the jhereg who can communicate with him through mind-speech. Vlad has been hired to kill a councilman named Mellar who has embezzled a huge sum of money from the Jhereg council. When Vlad catches up with Mellar, he discovers him hiding out in Castle Black, the floating mansion of Vlad’s friend, the Dragonlord Morrolan. Castle Black’s rule of hospitality is that anyone who has been invited to stay at the castle cannot be touched and nobody wants to violate this law because it would ignite another Dragon-Jhereg war. The last war devastated both houses. Vlad and Loiosh must flush out Mellar without offending a Dragonlord or starting a war. This is not an easy task and Vlad will need to solve a mystery and get a little help from his friends.<br /><br />Jhereg is appealing for several reasons. Vlad Taltos is a great character — the sort of honorable criminal that you can’t help but like. It helps that in Brust’s world, an assassination isn’t necessarily permanent. People can be revivified if their body is still mostly intact and they haven’t had their soul destroyed by a Morganti weapon (somewhat like Elric’s sword). Vlad is clever and must use his brain, not just his weapons or witchcraft, to solve his dilemma (though I thought he solved the convoluted mystery a little too easily). Vlad’s friends are also likeable, especially Loiosh the familiar, Vlad’s wife (who he met when she tried to kill him), and a female Dragonlord. Brust’s female characters are strong, smart, and competent.<br /><br />Steven Brust’s writing style, sense of humor, and dialogue are also pleasant, and the story moves quickly. There’s a lot to learn in the first novel of a huge epic, but Brust does this so well. We learn a little about Vlad’s childhood, the planet of Dragaera, the origin and structure of the houses (this was fascinating), and anything else we need to know. Brust gives us just enough extra to make us curious about his world, but not enough to make the plot slow down while we learn the entire history of Dragaera and its residents. (Yet, Brust’s world is so complex and detailed that some readers may wish for an online resource such as this helpful Wikipedia entry, and several fan-made Dragaera sites that you can easily find with a Google search.)<br /><br />Audible Frontiers’ version was narrated by Bernard Setaro Clark. He was terrific, speaking with a lively manner and giving each character a pleasant and distinct voice. As usual, I had to speed up the narration a bit (I’m beginning to suspect that Audible has purposely slowed down their narrators). I’m pleased to see that Bernard Setaro Clark has also narrated the sequels and I’ll be picking up book 2, Yendi, which is actually a prequel to Jhereg, very soon. I look forward to spending more time with Vlad Taltos.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11516950933393316701" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/112056983?book_show_action=true">Jul 17, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mike (the Paladin)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mike (the Paladin)" href="/user/show/2187043-mike-the-paladin">Mike (the Paladin)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780441385546" href="/book/show/1281575.Jhereg">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2187043-mike-the-paladin?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer112056983" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3217593107557224477">I've had this (and I believe 2 of the novels that follow it) on my shelves waiting to be read for years. I think I picked them up after I read Phoenix Guard...but, whatever prompted me to buy them they, like Dracula when he's staked but still a whole skeleton in his coffin, they were there... condemned to endless waiting. Happily this one was selected as the subject of a group read here on Goodreads, and I had a reason (excuse ?)to move it ahead of the huge pile of library books that are always </span>
  <span id="freeText3217593107557224477" style="display:none">I've had this (and I believe 2 of the novels that follow it) on my shelves waiting to be read for years. I think I picked them up after I read Phoenix Guard...but, whatever prompted me to buy them they, like Dracula when he's staked but still a whole skeleton in his coffin, they were there... condemned to endless waiting. Happily this one was selected as the subject of a group read here on Goodreads, and I had a reason (excuse ?)to move it ahead of the huge pile of library books that are always demanding my attention, waiting to be read...with a deadline date by which they must be returned. <br /><br />Now, bottom line? I liked it. This book is definitely what I'd call brain-candy...but that's okay. Novels are after all fiction and the vast majority are written and read simply for enjoyment, and this one is enjoyable. <br /><br />If you want the negatives I'd say that there are a few scenes where the book gets a little "wordy", some scenes that go on a bit too much in some description. But that's a small gripe.<br /><br />I will say that I was a bit surprised to find myself able to read at least somewhat sympathetically the character who is an assassin. But it held my interest and the character is written well. I found the world to be a bit "straining" in the suspension of reality department in maybe one point, but it is fantasy and again, in the end this is no big deal. On the whole the book works, the world works, and it all hangs together within the story.<br /><br />So again, I liked this book. Rating it, as I do especially in the case of light fiction or "brain-candy" books on enjoyment factor and how it held my interest...4 stars. I'd say I was going to run down and get the next book, but I already have it on my shelf...waiting. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3217593107557224477" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1175405196?book_show_action=true">Jan 20, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Eon ♒Windrunner♒  " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Eon ♒Windrunner♒  " href="/user/show/3481302-eon-windrunner">Eon ♒Windrunner♒  </a>

<div id="review_2658523020" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2658523020" />
    <a title="Daniel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/29777818-daniel"><img alt="Daniel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1523931823p2/29777818.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2658523020?book_show_action=true">Jan 05, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Daniel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Daniel" href="/user/show/29777818-daniel">Daniel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780441385522" href="/book/show/1410205.Jhereg">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29777818-daniel?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29777818-daniel?shelf=reread">reread</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29777818-daniel?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29777818-daniel?shelf=fantasy-noir">fantasy-noir</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2658523020" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2370056753559397154">Reread. To the best of my recollection I never reread this before now. I would have first read it in back in the 80s when it came out. I have no doubt 80s me loved it and would have given it five stars. For many years I counted Brust as one of my favorite authors, but the only books of his I reread were <i>To Reign In Hell</i> and <i>The Phoenix Guards</i>.<br/><br/>Somehow I drifted away from this series after five or six books, (I have six on my shelf), but I doubt very much that was a conscious decision.<br/><br/>2019 me is s</span>
  <span id="freeText2370056753559397154" style="display:none">Reread. To the best of my recollection I never reread this before now. I would have first read it in back in the 80s when it came out. I have no doubt 80s me loved it and would have given it five stars. For many years I counted Brust as one of my favorite authors, but the only books of his I reread were <i>To Reign In Hell</i> and <i>The Phoenix Guards</i>.<br /><br />Somehow I drifted away from this series after five or six books, (I have six on my shelf), but I doubt very much that was a conscious decision.<br /><br />2019 me is somewhat less enamored of the book at hand than I imagine 1980s me was, but rereading this 30+ years later is an interesting experience in itself. <br /><br />Coming back to this, I remembered only the vaguest details of the character and world, nothing of the particular story, other than it's the type of story that would come to dominate Urban Fantasy. (This book predates the blossoming of Urban Fantasy, but no doubt influenced it. Brust is associated with many of the early UF authors.)<br /><br />The writing in many ways is quite good for a first novel, better than some other authors' fifth or even tenth novels. Whether that's due to Brust's skill, or better editing back in the day before publishers decided editing was a good place to cut costs, I'm not sure. I suspect both.<br /><br />However, I initially wasn't sure this was going to be a successful reread. I had just bounced off an attempted reread of Lethem's <i>Gun, With Occasional Music</i>, and to be honest, the first thirty pages or so of this 239 page book were trying my patience as Brust piddled about establishing character and worldbuilding.<br /><br />As with much modern Urban Fantasy, there is a stink of wish fulfillment about this book. I can just picture a group of twelve year old boys coming up with Vlad: <i>He's gonna be an assassin! And a wizard! But not just a regular assassin, he's the boss assassin. And he's got a dragon! It's so cool!</i> It's a mini dragon. Basically a flying cat. I'm allergic to cats. Anyway, I'm sure I thought that was pretty cool when I was a teenage boy. Now I just find it kind of embarrassing. Which is totally my hang up, I'm not suggesting anyone else needs to be embarrassed about enjoying pet-dragon-having-assassins. But it's a very rare and special story that can take what I think of as juvenile targeted elements and slip past my defenses without triggering a cringe or two, and <i>Jhereg</i> doesn't quite manage it.<br /><br />After thirty pages the client shows up and the plot kicks off and it got substantially better. But not entirely better. Because <i>magic.</i><br /><br />Yes, that's me. The oddball fantasy reader who thinks magic is stupid. Feel free to stop paying attention, if you still are. <br /><br />Different writers handle magic in different ways, but this, sadly, is an example of the worst possible way. Early on, Vlad needs to locate his target and wants to do so with magic, but he can't. Because arbitrary nonsense. This whole sequence is basically pages of Star Trek Technobabble [TM]: The Magic Edition.<br /><br />It's like someone said you need to add more <i>obstacle, solution, complication</i> cycles and instead of thinking up some legitimate ones, he just set his characters down in a room and had them say:<br /><br />A: Obstacle!<br />B: Solution!<br />A: Complication!<br /><br />a few times, then padded it out with some magic terms.<br /><br />It's just insulting, really.<br /><br />The <i>find the target</i> bit is probably the worst of the magic related stuff, but there's some additional handwaving about the villain's motivation.<br /><br />I actually liked the plot, it's pretty strong if you can ignore the handwaving about the villain's motivation. The bit that was really annoying to me was that when Vlad finally figures out what the villain is up to, he basically figures it out by starting to think <i>more</i> racist.<br /><br />This book doesn't feature any of my ordinary fantasy bugbears, orcs, elves, vampires, etc. But it does divide people up into some distinct races. There's the easterners, of which Vlad is one, and presumably we're supposed to take as baseline human. Then there are the Dragaerans, which are divided up into seventeen "houses", sixteen of which were "genetically altered" to have traits of various local fauna by another long vanished race. The seventeenth house, the Jhereg, are made up of castoffs from other houses and mixed race people. The Jhereg incidentally, are basically the mob. It's unclear if there are any non-mobster Jhereg, or if there are any non-house-affiliated Dragaerans wandering around and how they live if so.<br /><br />Fantasy racism is no surprise to any fantasy reader, but this takes it to something of a new level in that when Vlad discovers the exact house mix of the Villain's ancestry suddenly he knows exactly what kind of person the villain is and how he thinks, and therefore the entire plot is laid bare due to the revelation of the villain's ancestry. I have no words... <br /><br />In addition to all the above, this book made me think about how common it is in fantasy books to have characters that are genocidal, or mass murderers, (Morrolan is said to have sacrificed entire villages to his god(dess?)), but they're okay really, because X. I mean, I'm all for complex characters and cultural context, but really?<br /><br />In any case, it seems like I've got a lot of gripes, but there's enough good here that I intend to reread more of the series and see how things change.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2370056753559397154" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Dan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/51021161-dan"><img alt="Dan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1507151305p2/51021161.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

<span id="freeTextContainer15504209354731965108">When I got this book, it sat on my shelf for quite a while. I knew nothing about the book, and just by the title and description, it sounded kinda lame. I finally picked it up, because it's a short one and I had just finished a massive book and needed something a little lighter.<br/><br/>So with that preamble, I can't tell you how surprised I was at how good this one is!   <span id="freeText15504209354731965108" style="display:none">When I got this book, it sat on my shelf for quite a while. I knew nothing about the book, and just by the title and description, it sounded kinda lame. I finally picked it up, because it's a short one and I had just finished a massive book and needed something a little lighter.<br /><br />So with that preamble, I can't tell you how surprised I was at how good this one is! It's fun as hell to read, and the characters are really great. Everything about this book is splendid. <br /><br />It almost reads like a detective novel, but only in parts. When the climax is being built, you get really into the planning phases, different possible scenarios, and it all really makes sense. This is edge of your seat kind of stuff.<br /><br />This is a solid 5 star book.</span>

<div id="review_1697149572" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1697149572" />
    <a title="Jack Lanigan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/49802347-jack-lanigan"><img alt="Jack Lanigan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1453928392p2/49802347.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1697149572?book_show_action=true">Jul 13, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jack Lanigan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jack Lanigan" href="/user/show/49802347-jack-lanigan">Jack Lanigan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1697149572" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2993001467587343063">I often make jokes in these reviews that I enjoy "nothing" books. Books where nothing happens. Slow paced books, introspective books, books with a slow build. Reading Jhereg, I have come to learn that things to happen in those books. Interesting things, things that move the story forward.<br/><br/>Jhereg is a book where nothing happens, and is incredibly dull about the whole thing.<br/><br/>Damn near every scene in this book features the main character slowly, and bored soundingly narrating (it was an audio version</span>
  <span id="freeText2993001467587343063" style="display:none">I often make jokes in these reviews that I enjoy "nothing" books. Books where nothing happens. Slow paced books, introspective books, books with a slow build. Reading Jhereg, I have come to learn that things to happen in those books. Interesting things, things that move the story forward.<br /><br />Jhereg is a book where nothing happens, and is incredibly dull about the whole thing.<br /><br />Damn near every scene in this book features the main character slowly, and bored soundingly narrating (it was an audio version so maybe that changes it) some menial thing about world building, or a more interesting story, or a future plan, and then he speaks to someone. Two or more people sit in a blank room and spout exposition about the history of the world, making sure to occasionally slip in a "well that's impossible", or "impressive, whoever came up with that idea must be a genius", or some other such auto-fellatioesque diatribe. Then the main character goes off to find the next character to speak to.<br /><br />And by god, what a dull main character he is. First person fantasy books have the advantage that the prose and exposition can be looked at in-character, or with a sense of difference to it. Vlad's dialogue makes him seem to be a smart-ass guy with impressive skills, but nearly all of the prose is drab, boring, ludicrously high-magic antics that remove any and all of the tension. Look at Dresden, or Fitz, or Jorg. That's how you do first person with a character.<br /><br />Not just that, but the world building that it so frequently leans on is just... boring. There are not-elves, descended from not-dragons, who use not-plot devices to do anything they want. Death is the most easily avoidable thing in the world and magic can, with enough thought and effort, do basically anything.<br /><br />It's just dull. Dull and bland and feels more like a first draft of every idea hurled at the wall to see what sticks, but the thing about a massive mess is that generally, lots of it is very sticky.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2993001467587343063" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1313874702" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1313874702" />
    <a title="Joel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8809317-joel"><img alt="Joel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1406312808p2/8809317.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1313874702?book_show_action=true">Jun 21, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joel" href="/user/show/8809317-joel">Joel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8809317-joel?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1313874702" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer563365001850767381">Jhereg is the tale of Vlad Taltos, an assassin who is a foreigner to his area, but has moved himself up in the organization of the Jhereg. Along with his companions, and his familiar Loiosh, a poisonous flying creature that he communicates with telepathically. Vlad is a sorcerer as well, capable of using his discouraged foreign magics to his power. He is approached by a daemon, who informs him of a board member of the controlling caste that took off with their entire fortune, and offers him an a</span>
  <span id="freeText563365001850767381" style="display:none">Jhereg is the tale of Vlad Taltos, an assassin who is a foreigner to his area, but has moved himself up in the organization of the Jhereg. Along with his companions, and his familiar Loiosh, a poisonous flying creature that he communicates with telepathically. Vlad is a sorcerer as well, capable of using his discouraged foreign magics to his power. He is approached by a daemon, who informs him of a board member of the controlling caste that took off with their entire fortune, and offers him an absurd amount of money to kill the man. <br /><br />Obviously, there's a lot more to it than that, but I'll leave it there as far as explanation goes. Jhereg is a very, very enjoyable little romp, with quite a bit of action including some somewhat-technical swordfighting. The worldbuilding is a bit sparse at times, but in the end a lot is revealed and fleshed out, and I left the book feeling as though I had a pretty good understanding of the world, characters and races, without ever feeling like there was an infodump or that I was being hit over the head by the information. <br /><br />It was an easy read, overall - Brust's prose is concise but not lacking, and is not overly complicated or flowery. The dialogue is enjoyable, characters are distinct and unique, the action and plot points well presented. He did not overuse the powers that the characters had, or use things like Loiosh as an "easy button" or "get out of jail free" card. There were tense moments, but i never felt like any characters were bailed out by a deus ex machina or anything along those lines. <br /><br />The book came highly recommended to me by many people as a fantasy in the 'assassin' mould - and I have to agree that it belongs near the top of that list. It wasn't perfect, and could have honestly used a tad more substance, perhaps more politics. That said, I liked it a lot, thought it was a fun read, and would continue in this series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="563365001850767381" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5999881-geoff?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1752291950" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5361976784037673842"><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/27704.Steven_Brust' title='Steven Brust' rel='nofollow noopener'>Steven Brust</a>'s first entry in his Vlad Taltos is an entertaining fantasy tale of assassination. <br/><br/>I was first made aware of this series when I read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17910076.What_Makes_This_Book_So_Great' title='What Makes This Book So Great by Jo Walton' rel='nofollow noopener'>What Makes This Book So Great</a> by <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/107170.Jo_Walton' title='Jo Walton' rel='nofollow noopener'>Jo Walton</a>. I didn't actually read the chapters on this series but her introduction to them was enough to pique my interest. <br/><br/>Brust almost introduces too much into the world in this first book. There's a long history that is teased in this novel but seems to have far reaching effects. There are 17 Great Houses of the empi</span>
  <span id="freeText5361976784037673842" style="display:none"><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/27704.Steven_Brust" title="Steven Brust" rel="nofollow noopener">Steven Brust</a>'s first entry in his Vlad Taltos is an entertaining fantasy tale of assassination. <br /><br />I was first made aware of this series when I read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17910076.What_Makes_This_Book_So_Great" title="What Makes This Book So Great by Jo Walton" rel="nofollow noopener">What Makes This Book So Great</a> by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/107170.Jo_Walton" title="Jo Walton" rel="nofollow noopener">Jo Walton</a>. I didn't actually read the chapters on this series but her introduction to them was enough to pique my interest. <br /><br />Brust almost introduces too much into the world in this first book. There's a long history that is teased in this novel but seems to have far reaching effects. There are 17 Great Houses of the empire, each having their own history &amp; traits, but only 3 (Dzur, Jhereg, Dragon) get any 'screen' time. And much more. Its a robust setup for the world in future novels, hopefully.<br /><br />But the story is straightforward. Vlad Taltos, assassin &amp; 'legitimate' business owner, gets hired to take out a noble who stole a very large amount of gold. From the start, Vlad knows it won't be an easy job, but, as the book progresses, it becomes clear that it will be difficulty for many larger reasons. And its his job to deal with it. <br /><br />I will definitely read the 2nd book, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/817357.Yendi__Vlad_Taltos___2_" title="Yendi (Vlad Taltos, #2) by Steven Brust" rel="nofollow noopener">Yendi</a>, but availability may be a problem.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2115317289" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2280929769438041551">Ages ago, I read Jo Walton’s reviews of the Vlad Taltos books and resolved to read them immediately. I did pick up this first book, but after that failed to carry on, even though the first book is good and Jo’s reviews fascinating. There’s a lot going on in this world, and I really want to read more of the books to get a better grasp on it. In the meantime, Vlad Taltos himself is snarky, moderately capable, and definitely capable of getting himself into trouble. A winning combination – even with</span>
  <span id="freeText2280929769438041551" style="display:none">Ages ago, I read Jo Walton’s reviews of the Vlad Taltos books and resolved to read them immediately. I did pick up this first book, but after that failed to carry on, even though the first book is good and Jo’s reviews fascinating. There’s a lot going on in this world, and I really want to read more of the books to get a better grasp on it. In the meantime, Vlad Taltos himself is snarky, moderately capable, and definitely capable of getting himself into trouble. A winning combination – even without Looish, his jhereg companion.<br /><br />It’s a fun beginning, which leaves a lot of questions unanswered (and sometimes even barely posed). This time, I mean it; I’ve gotta get on and read the rest!<br /><br /><a href="https://breathesbooks.com/2017/10/14/review-jhereg-2/" rel="nofollow noopener">Reviewed for The Bibliophibian.</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="2280929769438041551" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2137230572" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer138487271935220137">Brust does such a good job making these slim novels engaging and multifaceted. Fun capers, interesting character development and relationships, foreshadowing, meditations on free will and morality. Jhereg, while not the best in the series, is a very good book; there's a reason why this is the fourth or fifth time I've read it.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ZOP+HDDG1EHptVRl8lataPYFv3esMHr6t2kUG6upxZjFzt2Cu+fECr/nc6yzNUMb/htLkNGF242dr5y+N5oGpw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('3TqMdKUBULMcLyi3PH4LZ/hz0IGVimDqm20AQZwtr9B8F6/qLiBA+Ep9D359HeUU8G0kZug/wZ2xq4jkAB5s7w==')})
  }
//]]>

And finally, knowing his true identity, he acknowledges his true ambition - and resolves that the crown of Amber will be his.\n\nBut unknown to Corwin, there are dark forces massing against Amber... <span id="freeTextContainer5991388067905441150">Steven Karl Zoltán Brust (born November 23, 1955) is an American fantasy and science fiction author of Hungarian descent. He was a member of the writers' group The Scribblies, which included Emma Bull, Pamela Dean, Will Shetterly, Nate Bucklin, Kara Dalkey, and Patricia Wrede, and also belongs to the Pre-Joycean Fellowship.<br/><br/><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://us.macmillan.com/author/stevenbrust'>http://us.macmillan.com/author/steven...</a><br/><br/>(Photo by David Dyer-Bennet)</span>
